# PART T — Founder Idea Backlog (proposed 2026-07-06, NOT YET BUILT — analysis only, per explicit founder instruction: "DONT START BUILDING ANYTHING ELSE JUST ADD THEM IN THE FEATURES SECTION AND ANALYSE THEM CAREFULLY")

> **Standing instruction for whoever picks these up next**: every line below was investigated against the REAL current codebase before being written down — exact file paths, exact model/function names, and the exact real gap (not a guess) are cited so a future AI session does not have to re-discover any of this from scratch. Follow the project's standing rule: audit again yourself before writing code (the codebase moves fast; re-confirm nothing changed), then follow the strict CHUNK process (DB → Zod → service → API → UI → 4 UX states → seed) exactly like every other Part in this file, one idea/chunk at a time, never combined. Nothing in this Part has been scoped with the founder via `ask_user` yet — do that FIRST for each idea before writing any code, since several of these have real open design decisions flagged explicitly below.

## T.1 — Unique QR/Barcode PER PHYSICAL COPY of a library book (not just per-title)
- [ ] **The real gap, confirmed by direct code audit**: `LibraryBook.isbn` (`prisma/schema.prisma` ~line 1444) is unique PER TITLE per school (`@@unique([tenantId, isbn])`), and `copiesTotal` is just an integer count — there is currently NO way to tell physical copy #1 of "Facing Mount Kenya" apart from physical copy #7 of the same title; the existing `findByBarcode()` (`library.service.ts` line 135) scans/looks up by the shared title-level ISBN only. The founder's real request is a genuinely per-COPY identifier, so two books with the identical title (a common real case — schools buy multiples of set books) can each be tracked individually (which exact physical copy is out, with whom, condition, etc.), not just "how many of this title are currently out."
- [ ] **Real design decision needed before building (flag for `ask_user`)**: this requires either (a) a NEW child model, e.g. `LibraryBookCopy` (one row per physical copy, each with its own generated code, FK to the parent `LibraryBook`), replacing the current bare `copiesTotal` integer with real per-copy rows — the more correct long-term design, but a real migration that needs to backfill `copiesTotal` existing schools already have into real per-copy rows; or (b) a lighter-weight bolt-on that keeps `copiesTotal` as-is for schools that don't care about per-copy tracking, and adds an OPTIONAL parallel `LibraryBookCopy` table only for schools that opt into per-copy codes. Recommend confirming with the founder which one they want, since (a) is a bigger, more invasive change to a live model already used by fines/issues/digital-library, and B.15's existing regression tests would all need re-verification either way.
- [ ] **Real generation approach**: NEYO already has TWO real, working code-generation patterns to reuse rather than invent a third — (1) `DocumentVerification` (schema ~line 2560, `code String @unique`, already resolves a scanned code straight to a real entity via `studentId` for `docType: "student_id"`, N.2's exact pattern) is the more natural fit here: a new `docType: "library_copy"` row per physical copy, `studentId` left null, with a NEW `libraryBookCopyId` (or reuse `entityId`/`entityType` generically) added the same way N.2 added `studentId` — resolves a scan directly to the real copy, no fragile parsing. (2) `nextTenantId()`/`prefixFromSlug()` (`identity.service.ts`) is the OTHER real pattern already used for human-readable per-school codes (e.g. `KHS-LIB-000042`) if the founder wants a readable code printed under the QR rather than just the opaque `DocumentVerification.code`.
- [ ] **Real scanning infrastructure ALREADY EXISTS and should be reused, not rebuilt**: `qr-scan.service.ts` (N.2, `extractVerifyCode()`, `BarcodeDetector` browser API, USB handheld scanner support — "just types the decoded URL/code + Enter, no special hardware driver needed") already solves camera-scan AND USB-scanner input generically. The founder's explicit ask — "instead of putting the codes manually the qr codes or bar codes can be scanned" during issue — is a real, achievable extension of the EXISTING issue-book flow (`library.service.ts`'s `issueBook()`), swapping a manual book-search/pick for a scan-to-resolve step, mirroring N.2's exact UX pattern (scan → resolve → 1-tap action) rather than a new scanning system.
- [ ] **Real A4 print-sheet requirement, explicitly asking to "save on paper"**: the founder wants MANY small QR/barcode labels laid out on ONE A4 sheet (a real "print labels" layout, not one-code-per-page) so a school can cut+stick them onto books efficiently. NEYO already has a real `@react-pdf/renderer` document-generation system (`src/lib/documents/*.tsx` — e.g. `mzazi-card-pdf.tsx` already does A6 multi-page batch printing per class) as the pattern to follow, but a GRID-of-many-small-labels-per-single-page layout (not one-record-per-page) does not exist anywhere yet — this would be a genuinely new PDF layout, not a copy of an existing one. Real design decision to flag: label size/grid (e.g. Avery-style label sheet dimensions vs a plain grid), and whether the printed label includes just the QR or also the book title/copy number as human-readable text under it (recommended, for when a code fades/is damaged).
- [ ] **Bundi Intelligent library import — the founder's specific follow-up ask, ALREADY MOSTLY BUILT, only one real precise gap found**: N.1/N.2's `bundi-import.service.ts` already supports a real `domain: "LIBRARY"` import path (confirmed via direct code read, `commitSession()` branches to the real `importLibraryBatch()` for this domain) — importing a library register via a scanned/handwritten sheet is ALREADY REAL, not a gap. Per-copy code generation (T.1's own new capability above) would need to be wired into `importLibraryBatch()`/`libraryRowsFromTable()` (`library-import.service.ts`) so a bulk import can ALSO auto-generate a fresh per-copy code for every newly-created copy at import time — this specific wiring does not exist yet since per-copy tracking itself doesn't exist yet (see above), but once T.1's core model exists, this is a real, comparatively small addition to an already-working import pipeline, not a new import system.
- [ ] **The founder's separate ask — "importing library records even for alumni/current students for easier tracking" — is a REAL, PRECISE, narrower gap, confirmed via direct code audit**: `library.service.ts`'s `issueBook()` (line ~206) hard-filters borrowers to `status: "ACTIVE"` students only (`where: { id: input.studentId, status: "ACTIVE", deletedAt: null }`) — an alumni/graduated/transferred student's PAST borrowing history genuinely cannot be issued/tracked at all today, and bulk-importing a legacy paper library register that includes former students (a very real Kenyan-school scenario — many schools' existing paper ledgers span years of alumni) would hit this exact same active-only filter inside `importLibraryBatch()`'s reuse of the standard student-matching logic. Real fix shape: a school-configurable setting (or simply relaxing the status filter for IMPORT specifically, distinct from new day-to-day issuing) allowing `GRADUATED`/`TRANSFERRED` students to be valid, read-only "this book was historically issued to them" import targets — never allowing a NEW live issue to a non-active student, only import-time historical record-keeping. Needs `ask_user` to confirm the founder wants historical-only (no live re-issue to an alumnus) vs. also allowing an alumnus to be issued a NEW book (unusual, likely undesired — flag explicitly).

## T.2 — NEYO-Ops-Configured Discount Campaigns (new-user and/or platform-wide, with a start/end period)
- [ ] **The real gap, confirmed by direct code audit of every pricing/discount surface in the codebase**: `pricing-catalog.service.ts` (plans/add-ons pricing), `billing.service.ts` (subscribe/grandfathered-price logic), and `central-billing.service.ts` (NEYO's own subscription-collection webhook, Q.3-audited and since secured) all exist, but NONE of them has any concept of a time-boxed percentage discount, a coupon/promo code, or a "new signups only" rule. The closest REAL existing mechanisms are two structurally different, narrower things that should NOT be confused with this new idea: (1) `referral.service.ts`'s `processReferralRewards()` — a fixed 5% one-time reward, hardcoded, tied specifically to the referral-code mechanism, fires once on a referred school's first paid invoice; (2) `feature-grants.service.ts` (J.23 Revenue Grants) — grants a specific PREMIUM FEATURE to one named school for free, not a % off the base subscription price, and has no time window either (a grant just sits on/off until an Ops person manually revokes it — see the exact same JSON-in-`PlatformSetting` pattern S.2 reused for its own release gate, `neyo_feature_grants` key).
- [ ] **Founder's explicit two real use-cases to support**: (a) a discount for NEW schools only, auto-applied without any human process — "for new users it automatically uses the company rules and their discount is applied accordingly" — meaning a real rule engine NEYO Ops configures once (e.g. "20% off the first term for any school that signs up before 31 August"), that then applies itself automatically at the real moment a new school subscribes (`billing.service.ts`'s `subscribe()`), with zero manual step per school; (b) a discount NEYO Ops can apply to EVERYONE currently subscribed, for a defined period — a real, time-boxed platform-wide promotional window (e.g. "10% off all plans for the whole of December").
- [ ] **Real design shape to follow, reusing the codebase's own established patterns rather than inventing a new one**: model this as a new `PlatformSetting`-backed (or, if the founder wants a real audit-friendly history of past campaigns rather than just "the current one," a small new dedicated model, e.g. `DiscountCampaign` — a real Prisma migration) — either way, the SAME real shape as `pricing-catalog.service.ts`'s existing catalog-as-JSON pattern: `{ percentOff: number, appliesTo: "NEW_SIGNUPS" | "ALL_ACTIVE_SCHOOLS", startDate, endDate, active: boolean }`, likely allowing MULTIPLE simultaneous campaigns later (flag for `ask_user`: does the founder want to ever stack a "new user" discount with a separate "everyone" discount at the same time, or should only one campaign ever be active?). The real enforcement point for the "new users" case is `billing.service.ts`'s `subscribe()` (where `grandfatheredPrice` is already set — the discount would need to apply BEFORE that price is grandfathered-in, so the school's locked-in price already reflects the discount, not a separate line item bolted on after).
- [ ] **Real open questions to resolve via `ask_user` before building** (do NOT assume): does "new users" mean brand-new schools signing up for the FIRST time ever, or also includes a school reactivating after a lapsed subscription? Does the discount apply to the recurring per-term price forever (a genuinely discounted `grandfatheredPrice`), or only to the first term/payment (a one-time reduction, then reverting to full price after)? For the "everyone, for a period" case — does it apply automatically to a school's very next renewal that falls inside the window, or does it require every currently-subscribed school to be touched/re-billed immediately when the campaign starts? These materially change both the DB shape and the billing-job logic in `src/lib/jobs/registry.ts`'s subscription-related cron jobs and must be nailed down first.

## T.3 — School-Requested Custom Feature Pipeline (a real "request a custom feature" flow with NEYO-Ops-side pricing/approval/scoped access)
- [ ] **The real gap, confirmed by direct code audit**: no request/ticketing surface of ANY kind exists in the school-facing app for a school to ask NEYO for a bespoke feature — confirmed via a full grep for "request"/"custom feature"/"feature request" across `src/app` and `src/lib/services`, nothing found. The closest REAL adjacent systems, useful as building blocks but not the same thing: `feature-grants.service.ts` (J.23) already solves the LAST STEP of this idea perfectly — "give access to that school only" is EXACTLY what `setFeatureGrant()` already does (a real per-tenant JSON grant list, audit-logged) — once NEYO builds the custom feature and it needs its own feature key, granting it to just the requesting school is a solved problem, reuse it directly, don't rebuild it. `PlatformFlag` (G.22) is the existing mechanism for "pause something while we keep building it" — relevant if the custom feature is built as a real platform module first and then selectively released, mirroring exactly how Bundi (`bundi` module key) and Part-J features are staged today via `isJFeatureKey()`/`jFeatureKey()` in `src/lib/core/j-features.ts`.
- [ ] **What's genuinely NEW and needs building**: (1) a real school-facing "Request a custom feature" form (likely in Settings, gated on a leadership permission like `tenant.manage_settings`) where a school describes what they want; (2) a new real model (e.g. `CustomFeatureRequest`: tenantId, description, status `SUBMITTED → REVIEWING → QUOTED → APPROVED/DECLINED → IN_PROGRESS → DELIVERED`, a `quotedPriceKes` field, an Ops-only internal note field) — this is genuinely new, no existing model fits; (3) a real NEYO Ops console view (a new tab in `founder-ops-client.tsx`, following the exact same list-with-status-badges-and-actions pattern already used by `RevenueGrantsOpsTab`/`ShellReleaseCard`) where NEYO reviews requests, sets a quoted price, and marks status; (4) the school sees the quoted price + status back in their own Settings once NEYO responds — a real, if lightweight, two-way workflow (not just a one-way "contact us" form that goes nowhere trackable).
- [ ] **Real open question to resolve via `ask_user`**: once a custom feature is actually BUILT (by a human engineer/future AI session, not automated), how should NEYO Ops "give access to that school only" — a bespoke new `PlatformFlag`/module key built specifically for that one school's feature (reusing G.22's exact real pattern), or should ALL custom one-off features route through the EXISTING generic `feature-grants.service.ts` J.23 grant system instead of minting a new flag per custom feature? The latter is likely cleaner (one real mechanism, not N one-off flags) but needs the founder's confirmation since J.23's `REVENUE_FEATURE_KEYS` list is currently a small, curated, pre-defined set (`src/lib/core/revenue-features.ts`) — a custom one-off feature per school doesn't naturally fit a small enumerated list model unless that list is made open-ended.

## T.4 — Duplicate Human-Readable School ID Prefixes (e.g. "Kahawa High School" and "Kirinyaga High School" both → "KHS") — real risk analyzed, root cause confirmed, NOT a data-integrity bug
- [ ] **Direct confirmation of the founder's exact concern, traced through the real code**: `prefixFromSlug()` (`src/lib/core/identity.ts` line 36) takes the first letter of each of the first 3 words of a school's slug — "Kahawa High School" → K,H,S → literally the string `"KHS"`; "Kirinyaga High School" → K,H,S → the SAME literal string `"KHS"`. `nextTenantId()` (`identity.service.ts`) then builds every human-facing ID as `${prefix}${entityCode}${number}` — e.g. a student ID `KHS5`. **Confirmed: yes, two genuinely different real schools CAN and WILL produce the identical human-readable prefix if their first 3 words start with the same letters** — this is real, not a hypothetical.
- [ ] **Confirmed this does NOT cause any actual data corruption or cross-tenant leakage — the underlying database uniqueness is correctly scoped per-tenant, not by the human-readable string**: every real entity table that stores one of these generated IDs enforces uniqueness as `@@unique([tenantId, admissionNo])` (Student, `prisma/schema.prisma` line 3589) or `@@unique([tenantId, invoiceNo])` (Invoice, line 585) — the ACTUAL database key is always `(tenantId, humanId)` together, never the human ID alone. `IdSequence`'s own counter (line 3277, `@@unique([tenantId, entityType])`) is likewise scoped per-tenant. So "KHS5" at Kahawa High and "KHS5" at Kirinyaga High are two completely distinct, correctly-isolated real database rows — A.2's tenant isolation (`tenantDb()`/`withTenant()`) means neither school can ever see or query the other's data regardless of the human ID string colliding. **This is a real, confirmed, narrow display/readability risk, not a security or data-integrity bug.**
- [ ] **Where the real (limited) risk genuinely does show up, confirmed by checking every cross-tenant-visible surface**: (1) NEYO Ops / SUPER_ADMIN views that list or search across MULTIPLE real schools at once (e.g. the `founder-ops-client.tsx` schools dropdowns used by `RevenueGrantsOpsTab`/`ShellReleaseCard`) show the real school NAME alongside any ID, so a human operator is not actually at risk of confusing "KHS5" from one school with "KHS5" from another IF they're reading the school name too — but a raw exported ID list (e.g. a CSV export via `tenant.export_data`) that shows ONLY the human ID column without a school-name column alongside it could genuinely be ambiguous once combined outside NEYO (e.g. two spreadsheets from two different schools, both mentioning "KHS5", accidentally merged by a third party); (2) R.4's real multi-school parent feature (`multi-school.service.ts`) — a parent legitimately switching between two schools that happen to share a prefix would see the identical-looking ID format on both, though the `SchoolSwitcher` UI always shows the real distinct school NAME at the point of switching, so the same "as long as the name is shown alongside" mitigation applies; (3) any future printed/physical document context where a physical card/paper from two schools with colliding prefixes could sit side-by-side (e.g. two neighboring schools in the same county, a real plausible Kenyan scenario) — the G.9 co-branded document system (logo, brand colors, school name header) already puts the real school's name/logo prominently on every generated document (invoices, ID cards, receipts, report cards), so this again mitigates but does not fully eliminate visual-only confusion for someone glancing at just the ID code.
- [ ] **Real, NOT-YET-BUILT fix options to consider, with tradeoffs, for when the founder wants this addressed** (none implemented — this section is analysis only): (a) **detect + auto-disambiguate at slug-creation time** — when a new school signs up (`onboarding.service.ts`'s `signupSchool()`) and its computed prefix already exists among OTHER real tenants, append a real numeric/letter suffix (e.g. the second "KHS" school becomes "KHS2" or "KH2") — a real, fully backward-compatible fix (existing schools' IDs never change) that only affects brand-new signups going forward, likely the lowest-risk real option; (b) **let a school pick/edit their own prefix explicitly during onboarding** (currently 100% auto-derived from the slug with no override) — more founder/customer control, but needs real validation against uniqueness at signup time and a real UI step that doesn't exist today; (c) **do nothing structurally and rely on the existing real name/logo mitigations above**, since the underlying data is provably safe — a real, valid choice if the founder decides visual-only ambiguity across unrelated schools' printed documents is an acceptable, low-frequency real-world risk. Recommend `ask_user` to pick between (a)/(b)/(c) before writing any code, since (a) and (b) are both real, non-trivial changes to the live onboarding flow that need their own full CHUNK process and regression testing (including confirming existing tenants' IDs are never touched).

## T.5 — Background Task Runner (long jobs continue while browsing elsewhere) + Picture-in-Picture
- [ ] **The real gap, confirmed by direct code audit**: NEYO already has a REAL background job system — `src/lib/jobs/registry.ts` (BullMQ-backed when Redis is configured via the vault, in-process fallback otherwise — A.12), used today for cron-scheduled work (fee reminders, term pulse, data retention, etc.) and for the Bundi Intelligent pipeline's OCR/AI-escalation steps. What does NOT exist: a real, VISIBLE, user-facing "this is running in the background, come back to it later" affordance FOR A USER-INITIATED action they kicked off themselves (e.g. a big bulk import, a bulk PDF generation, a whole-school timetable regeneration) — today, several of these long operations (`timetable-engine.service.ts`'s `runGeneration()`, large Bundi Intelligent imports, bulk PDF batch generation) either block the UI with a spinner until done, or run as a fire-and-forget job the user has no live-progress visibility into unless they stay on that exact page. Confirmed via grep: no `JobRun`-linked persistent "notification when done" pattern surfaced generically across the app (the closest real analog is P.6's `TimetableGenerationJob`, which does track real background job status, but is timetable-specific, not a generic "any long task" pattern).
- [ ] **Real, reusable building blocks that already exist and should be extended, not replaced**: `A.7`'s real notification cascade (`notify()`, in-app bell + push/SMS/email) already has everything needed to tell a user "your [X] finished" the moment a background job completes, wherever they've navigated to since — this is likely the core of a real fix: make every long-running, user-initiated job create a real `JobRun`-style row (the pattern already exists per A.12) and fire a real in-app notification via the EXISTING `notify()` cascade on completion, rather than requiring the user to babysit a spinner on one page. A generic "Background Tasks" indicator (a persistent small icon/badge in the Topbar showing "2 tasks running", clickable to see real progress) would be a genuinely new UI component, but the underlying job-tracking plumbing (`JobRun`/similar) already exists and just needs to be applied MORE broadly across long user-triggered actions, not built from scratch.
- [ ] **Picture-in-picture — real, distinct, and narrower than "background tasks"**: PiP is a specific browser API (`documentPictureInPicture`/the older video-only `requestPictureInPicture`) for keeping a small floating window visible while a user browses OTHER tabs/apps outside the browser entirely — genuinely different from an in-app background-task notification. Confirmed via grep: zero references to PiP anywhere in the codebase today. The most plausible real NEYO use case, given what already exists: the real NEYO Intercom/live-call feature (`intercom.service.ts`, `DashboardIntercomClient`, reused inside S.1/S.2's `ShellSidePanel`) or the real WebRTC online-class rooms (Q.3-audited `online-class-room-client.tsx`) — a PiP mini-window showing "still on a call/class" while a user navigates elsewhere in NEYO (or even switches to a different browser tab entirely) would be the natural, real fit, not a generic app-wide feature. Needs `ask_user` to confirm which specific real feature(s) the founder wants PiP applied to, since building a generic "any page can PiP" capability with no concrete target is far vaguer than wiring it to one or two specific, already-real live-call surfaces.
- [ ] **"Any other thing maybe" — founder's own open invitation, not scoped further; genuinely deferred until the founder gives a more specific example.**

## T.6 — Influencer/Promoter Marketing Codes (distinct from the existing school-to-school Referral system)
- [ ] **The real gap, confirmed by direct code audit, and the real, important distinction from what ALREADY EXISTS**: `referral.service.ts` (already built, live) is SCHOOL-to-SCHOOL only — `ensureReferralCode()`/`applyReferralCode()`/`processReferralRewards()` all operate on `Tenant` rows (`Tenant.referralCode`, `Tenant.referredByTenantId`, `Tenant.hasClaimedReferral`), a fixed hardcoded 5%, one-time, both sides rewarded equally, with NO separate "influencer" identity at all — a referral code today IS a school's own code, there is no concept of a real individual PERSON (not a school) holding a code and earning an ongoing/tracked payout. The founder's idea is genuinely different and additional: a real INDIVIDUAL (an influencer/promoter, not a customer school) gets their own unique code; when ANY school uses it, that school gets a discount AND the influencer separately earns their own agreed reward "on top of salary agreed" — implying influencers may be real NEYO staff/contractors with a base pay PLUS this variable commission, a genuinely different real financial relationship than the existing school-referring-school reward.
- [ ] **What's genuinely NEW and needs building, since no part of this exists today**: a new real model, e.g. `InfluencerCode` (a real person's name/contact, their unique code, a configurable discount % for the school that uses it, a configurable commission — flat KES or % — owed to the influencer per school that signs up through them, real running-total tracking of schools referred + total commission earned/paid), distinct from `Tenant.referralCode`. A real NEYO Ops UI to create/manage influencer codes and see each one's real performance (schools signed up, revenue generated, commission owed/paid) — a genuinely new console view, likely modeled visually on the existing `RevenueGrantsOpsTab`/`ShellReleaseCard` list-based pattern for consistency, but backed by wholly new data since `Tenant`-only referral fields don't fit a non-tenant person. A real "commission owed" ledger/payout-tracking mechanism — the founder said "the company can have," implying NEYO pays the influencer directly (a real payable NEYO owes, likely needs its own simple ledger — not necessarily full payroll-grade, but at minimum a real "amount owed, amount paid, when" record NEYO Ops can mark as settled).
- [ ] **Real open questions to resolve via `ask_user`**: is an influencer code applied at the SAME moment/mechanism as the existing school referral code (i.e., does `applyReferralCode()` get extended to accept EITHER a school code OR an influencer code, or is this a fully separate, parallel code-entry field during signup)? Does a school's influencer-code discount stack with any other real discount from T.2's campaign system, or are they mutually exclusive (a real business rule the founder needs to decide, since combining both could compound into an unintended large discount)? Is the influencer's own reward a ONE-TIME payment per school signed (mirroring the existing referral reward's one-time-on-first-payment trigger) or an ONGOING percentage of that school's subscription revenue for as long as they remain subscribed (a much bigger, recurring financial commitment, and a materially different calculation to build) — this is the single biggest open design fork and must be nailed down before any schema work starts.

## T.7 — Configurable Fee Structure Modes: Per-Class vs. One School-Wide Structure
- [ ] **Real audit finding: this is LARGELY ALREADY BUILT, a smaller gap than it first appears** — `FeeStructure` (`prisma/schema.prisma` line 532) already has BOTH a `level` field (class-level-wide) AND an optional `classId` override (`classId String?`, "optional exact class/stream override (I.35)") with a real compound uniqueness constraint `@@unique([tenantId, level, year, term, classId])` — meaning a school can ALREADY define either one shared fee structure per level (leaving `classId` null) or a distinct one per exact class/stream (setting `classId`), and `batchInvoice()` (`finance.service.ts`) already correctly prefers an exact-class-match structure over a level-wide one when both exist (confirmed via the fallback lookup logic reused across R.8's own recent work in the same file). **The founder's "one fee structure for the whole school" case (a single flat fee regardless of class) is the one real, narrower gap**: today a school MUST create at least one `FeeStructure` per class `level` string (e.g. separately for "Form 1", "Form 2", "Form 3", "Form 4") even if every level pays the exact identical amount — there is no single "whole-school, all-levels" structure shortcut; a school with a genuinely flat fee still has to create N duplicate-content structures, one per level, which is real (if minor) extra admin work, not a missing capability.
- [ ] **Real, small proposed fix** (not built): allow `FeeStructure.level` to accept a real sentinel value (e.g. `"ALL"` or a new `applyToAllLevels: Boolean` flag) that `batchInvoice()`'s class-lookup (`finance.service.ts`) treats as matching every class regardless of level — a genuinely small, additive change to an already-solid, well-tested system (confirmed still covered by `scripts/i35-fees-logic-test.ts` and `scripts/finance-test.ts`, both currently green) rather than a new system. Needs `ask_user` to confirm this exact interpretation matches what the founder means by "one fee structure," since an alternative reading is "one INVOICE covering multiple fee types together" (already fully solved today via `FeeItem` — multiple line items per structure, e.g. Tuition + Boarding + Activity all under one structure) — worth explicitly re-confirming which of these two real, different things the founder is actually asking for before writing any code.

## T.8 — Transport: Student-Enrollment-Time Route/Shift/Vehicle Auto-Allocation, Route-Change Requests, Seat-Reclaim, and Mid-Term Cost Adjustment — **FULLY BUILT** (founder-requested 2026-07-06/07, "head on to Part T START THE FULL BUILD" — the biggest, most structurally significant Part T item, built first per the founder's own "DO THE BIGGER ONES FIRST PLEASE")
- [x] **Real audit before any code**: confirmed the pre-Part-T system was a genuinely solid, already-tested foundation (one `TransportRoute` ↔ one `Vehicle`/`Driver`, capacity-checked `assignStudent()`, pickup-stop validation, idempotent `invoiceRiders()`) — every founder-flagged gap below was real and confirmed via direct code/grep audit, never assumed.
- [x] **Real `TransportShift` child model** (migration `20260707134916_t8_transport_shifts_and_route_requests`, a genuine additive `CREATE TABLE` + a real `RedefineTables` on `Tenant`/`TransportAssignment` preserving every existing row via `INSERT...SELECT`, zero data loss) — one route can now run multiple real, separately-vehicled/driven shifts (e.g. "Morning"/"Afternoon"), each with its own optional `vehicleId`/`driverId`, a real school-chosen `seatCapOverride` (founder's own "a school can customize the seats number to their liking too" ask — independent of the vehicle's own physical capacity), and an optional `termFeeKesOverride`. **Fully backward-compatible**: a route with zero real shifts keeps working exactly as before (its own direct `vehicleId` fallback), confirmed via a dedicated regression path proving the legacy shape is untouched.
- [x] **Real automatic seat allocation at enrollment time** (`autoAllocateStudent()`) — founder's own confirmed tie-break rule: the caller picks the ROUTE, the system finds every real shift on it with a free seat and picks the one with the MOST free seats first (a real, simple, honest rule, never a black box); if every real shift is genuinely full, it throws a real, honest `FULL` error naming the route and telling the caller a new shift is needed — it NEVER silently overbooks or silently redirects to a different route the caller didn't ask for. Falls back to the legacy direct-`assignStudent()` path for a route with zero shifts.
- [x] **Real seat-reclaim notification** — the moment `releaseAssignment()` frees a seat, every real `SCHOOL_OWNER`/`PRINCIPAL`/`DEPUTY_PRINCIPAL` staff member is notified ("Transport seat freed up... [route] — [shift]") — live-verified: a real Achieng release fired 2 real notification rows referencing the exact real route freed.
- [x] **Real, shift-fee-aware invoicing** — `invoiceRiders()` now bills each real rider at their OWN real shift's `termFeeKesOverride` if one is set, else falls back to the route's own default fee (the exact pre-existing behavior, unchanged for schools that never set shift-level fees); the pre-existing "reject a genuinely fee-less route" guard (`route.termFeeKes` OR at least one real per-shift override must be > 0) was restored after a real regression was caught by the project's own pre-existing `transport-test.ts` mid-build and fixed before merge.
- [x] **Real parent-portal-initiated route/shift change requests** (`TransportRouteChangeRequest` model) — gated by a real, explicit school-level opt-in toggle (`Tenant.allowParentTransportRequests`, default `false`); a parent can request a new route (and optionally a specific shift/pickup stop + a free-text reason) for their OWN child only, enforced via the exact same `assertOwnChild()` row-scoping guard every other parent-portal action in `parent-portal.service.ts` already uses — live-verified a parent genuinely cannot request a change for another family's real child, and genuinely cannot submit anything at all while the school toggle is off (`FORBIDDEN`, not silently accepted).
- [x] **Real, school-CHOSEN mid-term billing rule** (`Tenant.transportMidTermBillingRule`, default `"NEXT_TERM_ONLY"`) — founder's own explicit resolution: "a school choses what they would like in their system", never a fixed platform-wide behavior. Three real modes, all live-verified end to end via `decideRouteChangeRequest()`: **`TOPUP`** — a real full manual invoice for the new route/shift's fee is created immediately (live-verified: a real KES 9,000 invoice `KHINV302` genuinely appeared on Achieng's real ledger the moment a TOPUP-mode approval fired); **`PRORATE`** — a real pro-rated invoice is computed from the real current `AcademicTerm`'s genuine remaining days (`Math.round(fee × remainingDays / totalDays)`), or an honest `DEFERRED_TO_NEXT_TERM` if zero real term-days remain or no current term exists — never a fabricated number; **`NEXT_TERM_ONLY`** (the safe default) — takes no billing action now and honestly records `billingActionTaken: "DEFERRED_TO_NEXT_TERM"` with an explanatory note. Every decision leaves a real, permanent, auditable `billingActionTaken`/`billingNote` record on the request row — never silent.
- [x] **CHUNK 5/6 — Real staff-facing UI**, extending the pre-existing `transport-client.tsx` (never duplicated, always extended): real per-route shift badges on the Routes tab (live seat/fee at a glance); a new "Shifts" board per route (create/edit/archive a shift, with real duplicate-name and real "can't archive with live riders" guards surfaced honestly in the UI); the Riders-board "Add rider" dialog now offers a real auto-allocate checkbox (default ON) or manual shift picker (full shifts shown disabled, never silently selectable); a new fourth "Requests" tab — a real staff queue showing real human-readable student/route/shift names (never raw IDs), a real live preview of "Billing if approved" driven by the school's own current setting, and real Approve/Decline actions (decline supports an optional free-text reason shown back to the parent); a new "Transport settings" panel (billing-rule picker + the parent-request opt-in toggle, with real, honest copy explaining what each does).
- [x] **CHUNK 5/6 — Real parent-portal UI** — new `TransportRequestCard` component, wired into the existing `ChildView` in `parent-portal-client.tsx` (never a new page — extends the established card-based child-detail pattern): shows the child's real current route/shift/pickup-stop, a real "Request a route/shift change" action (hidden — not just disabled — when the school hasn't opted in, replaced with an honest "contact the school office" message), a real dialog to pick a new route (+ optional shift, showing real live seat availability per shift, full ones disabled) and an optional reason, and a real history list of the parent's own past requests with their real decided status/decline reason/billing outcome.
- [x] **Real bug found and fixed mid-build, unrelated to T.8 but blocking live verification, investigated and fixed rather than routed around**: `GET /api/portal/parent/pathway` (J.10) was double-wrapping its response body (`ok({ data })` around a service function that already returns `{ student, pathways }` directly), causing every real parent-portal page load to throw a genuine client-side `Cannot read properties of undefined (reading 'length')` inside the pre-existing, unrelated `ParentPathwayCard` component — confirmed via a real Playwright console/pageerror capture against the dev server, confirmed via `git diff` that this route was untouched by any of this session's own T.8 work, and fixed with a single-line, surgical `return ok(data)` correction (matching the response shape the pre-existing component genuinely expects).
- [x] **Real CSS-positioning bug found and fixed in the new T.8 parent-portal dialog**: the new `RequestDialog` (a real `position: fixed` full-viewport overlay) was initially rendered as a JSX child INSIDE the pre-existing `<Card>` component, whose own `hover:-translate-y-0.5` CSS transform silently became the dialog's containing block — breaking full-viewport centering (confirmed via a real, non-cropped Playwright screenshot showing the dialog rendering as a faint overlay clipped to the card's own bounds instead of centered over the page). Fixed by moving the dialog to render as a SIBLING of `<Card>` (matching the exact pattern the pre-existing `PickupPersonDialog`/`AltPickupDialog` already use one file up) — re-verified via a fresh Playwright screenshot showing the dialog correctly centered and fully legible.
- [x] **CHUNK 8 — Real seed data**: Karibu High's existing Route A ("Kasarani") was split into two real demo shifts — "Morning" (06:30–07:15, bus KCB 123A, no seat-cap override, carries the 2 pre-existing real riders Wanjiru + Kiprono) and "Afternoon" (16:00–16:45, same real bus, a real custom 20-seat cap deliberately smaller than the bus's own 33-seat physical capacity, left genuinely empty for a realistic auto-allocate demo). Achieng (the seeded PARENT-login demo child) was moved onto Route B ("Githurai", the legacy no-shifts route, picking up at Githurai 45) specifically to prove real backward compatibility live. `Tenant.allowParentTransportRequests` was seeded `true` so the founder can screenshot/demo the parent-portal request flow immediately without a manual settings toggle first. `npm run db:seed` run twice — byte-identical shift/assignment counts confirmed via direct DB re-query both times (idempotent, no duplication).
- [x] **New `scripts/t8-transport-shifts-test.ts`** — 20 real assertions against the real DB (`scripts/_assert.ts` harness, cleanup in a `finally` block before `summary()`/`process.exit()`): real shift CRUD (create/update/seat-cap-override/duplicate-name-blocked/archive-blocked-while-riders-present); real shift-aware `assignStudent()` (a shifted route demands a real `shiftId`, a legacy route still doesn't); real capacity enforcement on a shift; real `autoAllocateStudent()` picking the most-free-seats shift and honestly throwing `FULL` when every real shift is genuinely full; real seat-reclaim notification firing on release; real shift-fee-aware `invoiceRiders()` billing the correct per-shift override amount; the full real request→decide lifecycle for ALL THREE billing rules (NEXT_TERM_ONLY/TOPUP/PRORATE) plus a real decline path proving nothing is silently changed; real `FORBIDDEN` rejection while the school opt-in is off; real row-scoping proving a parent cannot request a change for another family's real child (Kamau, a genuinely different real guardian); real human-readable staff-queue name resolution; real parent-portal-info/history row-scoping. Run twice consecutively — **20/20 passed both times**, full cleanup confirmed via direct DB re-query (0 leftover test students/routes/vehicles/requests, settings restored to the exact pre-test values).

- [ ] **No GPS bus tracking** — remains hardware-deferred exactly as B.17 originally flagged; never faked.

## T.9 — Cafeteria/Feeding Program: School-Wide vs. Per-Class Cost, Opt-Out/Opt-In Students, Mid-Term Portal Self-Enrollment
- [ ] **The real current system, confirmed by direct code audit** (`MealCard` model, `prisma/schema.prisma` line 1907, cafeteria.service.ts): a `MealCard` is issued PER STUDENT, individually, by staff — `planName`/`meals`/`termFeeKes` are all set per card at issue time, and issuing ALREADY correctly creates a real B.7 invoice first (the founder's own standing "every chargeable service bills the student's invoice" rule, confirmed already enforced here). **What's real and already solved**: per-student, staff-issued meal billing with real invoicing. **What's genuinely NOT solved, confirmed by the same audit**: there is no concept of a school-wide DEFAULT feeding cost derived from class level (the founder's "put the required feeding cost either per class or per school depending on the school" — closest existing analog is `FeeStructure`'s real per-level/per-class shape, T.7 above, but `MealCard` has no equivalent link to `FeeStructure`/class-level pricing at all today — it's a fully separate, manually-typed `termFeeKes` per card, every time); there is no "all students eat, therefore auto-issue everyone a card at term-invoicing time" bulk mode (contrast with B.7's own `batchInvoice()`, which DOES auto-invoice an entire class level in one action — cafeteria has no equivalent bulk action); there is no parent/teacher self-service enrollment into the feeding program via the portal (confirmed via the same `parent-portal.service.ts` grep as T.8 — zero cafeteria-related self-service functions exist).
- [ ] **Real, structurally similar problem to T.8's transport self-enrollment ask** — the founder explicitly wants the SAME capability (self-service enrollment mid-term, with a school-configurable "can students join anytime" toggle) for BOTH transport AND feeding, so these two ideas should very likely be designed and built together, sharing the same real self-service-request pattern in the parent portal + the same "school allows / doesn't allow mid-term enrollment" toggle concept, rather than as two unrelated one-off builds — flag this connection explicitly for whoever scopes T.8/T.9 next.
- [ ] **Real open question, same shape as T.8's mid-term-transport-cost question**: what happens to feeding cost when a student's class-level default fee changes (the founder says "the fees and costs updates automatically with the classes") — does this mean a student's ALREADY-ISSUED `MealCard` for the current term should be treated as locked at issue time (the current real behavior — a term fee stored on the card doesn't change once issued), or does the founder want an ACTIVE card's cost to dynamically follow a live class-level default even mid-term (a materially different, more complex real behavior requiring `MealCard` to reference a live `FeeStructure`-like source rather than storing its own frozen `termFeeKes`)? This is a real, consequential design fork — needs `ask_user` before any schema change.

## T.10 — Teacher Portal: Cash Payments Pending School Confirmation
- [ ] **The real gap, confirmed by direct code audit of the real permission matrix** (`src/lib/core/permissions.ts`): `finance.record_payment` — the real permission `recordWalkInPayment()`/`applyPaymentToInvoice()` require — is granted today to `BURSAR`, `ACCOUNTANT`, and `RECEPTIONIST` (and, implicitly, leadership roles via `FINANCE_FULL`), but explicitly NOT to `TEACHER`/`CLASS_TEACHER` at all — confirmed by reading the full `ROLE_PERMISSIONS` map. The founder's ask — "a teacher when a school allows can allow cash payments in their portals and it can only be confirmed by the school" — is NOT simply "grant teachers `finance.record_payment`" (which would let a teacher-recorded payment apply and print a receipt immediately, same as a bursar, undermining the explicit "only be confirmed by the school" trust boundary the founder is asking for) — it requires a genuinely NEW real state, a pending/unconfirmed cash entry a teacher can create but which does NOT touch the real invoice ledger (does not mark PAID, does not trigger R.5's automatic receipt-to-portal delivery, does not fire a receipt SMS) until a real bursar/leadership user explicitly confirms it.
- [ ] **Real design shape to follow, reusing existing patterns rather than inventing a wholly new state machine**: the codebase already has a real "pending → later confirmed by someone else" shape in at least two places worth modeling this on: (1) B.25 Procurement's `PurchaseOrder`/expense approval-threshold pattern (`createExpense`/`createOrderFromQuote` auto-approve under a threshold, else `PENDING_APPROVAL`, with a real `approveExpense()`/`rejectExpense()` step gated to leadership, self-approval explicitly blocked) — directly analogous shape: a teacher's cash entry could sit in a new `PENDING_CONFIRMATION` status until a real bursar/leadership approves it, at which point (and only then) the REAL `recordWalkInPayment()` fires with all its existing real side effects (R.3 biometric gate if enabled, R.5 receipt delivery, print-queue auto-print) — meaning this is best built as a thin NEW pre-step in FRONT of the fully-real, already-battle-tested `recordWalkInPayment()`, not a parallel payment-recording system; (2) R.6's `waiveActivityParticipant()`/`unwaiveActivityParticipant()` pattern (a real, deliberately narrow function that is the ONLY path allowed to create a specific kind of exception state) is a useful reference for how to keep a new "teacher-submitted, unconfirmed" state narrowly scoped and auditable.
- [ ] **Real open questions for `ask_user`**: should this be a school-level toggle (mirroring R.3's `Tenant.requireBiometricForFinance` on/off pattern exactly) so schools that don't want teachers touching cash at all can leave it off entirely — almost certainly yes, given the founder's own "when a school allows" phrasing; should a teacher's pending cash entry require the SAME R.3 biometric gate a bursar's real payment would (likely yes, for consistency, if the school has that gate on); what happens if a bursar REJECTS a teacher-submitted cash entry (does the teacher get notified, is there a reason field, does anything get logged for later dispute resolution) — none of this exists as a pattern anywhere else in the codebase today and needs real decisions before building.

## T.11 — School-Configurable Fee-Reminder Schedule/Limits + "Never Logged In" Parent SMS Nudge Campaign
- [ ] **Real current reminder system, confirmed by direct code audit** (`sendFeeReminders()`, `finance.service.ts` line 532, scheduled via `src/lib/jobs/registry.ts`): reminders run on a FIXED, hardcoded 3-day dedupe window (`reminderSentAt`), triggered by a fixed cron schedule — there is NO school-configurable "how often" or "starting how many days overdue" setting anywhere; every school gets the identical fixed cadence today. The founder's ask — "a school can set their fees reminder dates and limits so that sometimes it just becomes an automatic process" — is a real, clean, well-scoped gap: add real school-level settings (e.g. `Tenant.feeReminderDedupeDays`, `Tenant.feeReminderGraceDays` before the first reminder fires) that `sendFeeReminders()` reads instead of its current hardcoded `threeDaysAgo` constant — a genuinely small, additive change to an already-working, already-tested (via the pre-existing reminder-adjacent regression coverage) real system, not a rebuild.
- [ ] **The "never logged in" / "long-inactive" parent SMS nudge — a REAL, GENUINELY NEW capability, confirmed nothing like it exists**: grep across `src/lib/services` and `src/lib/jobs` for any "inactive user" / "never logged in" detection found nothing — no existing job or report identifies parents whose `Session` history shows zero real logins ever, or whose last real login is older than some threshold. This is buildable with data that already exists (the real `Session` model, already used correctly by A.1's login system and R.4's multi-school switching) — a new real query (e.g. `db.session.findMany` grouped by `userId`, or simpler: track a real `User.lastLoginAt` timestamp, which does NOT currently exist as a column and would need one) — but the actual SMS-nudge job/report itself, and any UI surfacing "N parents have never logged in, send them a nudge?" to a bursar/principal, is genuinely new, not an extension of `sendFeeReminders()` (a different real trigger — inactivity, not fee overdue — even though it reuses the SAME real A.7 SMS-sending cascade underneath).
- [ ] **Real design note**: these two ideas (T.11's two halves) are related in spirit (both are "make routine SMS outreach more automatic/configurable") but are structurally TWO separate real features — recommend scoping and building them as two distinct chunks even if done in the same session, since one extends an existing job (reminder cadence) and the other requires a genuinely new detection mechanism (login-activity tracking) plus a new `User.lastLoginAt`-style column and its own new job.

## T.12 — Leave Management Linked to the Timetable: Substitute Teacher Proposals — **FULLY BUILT** (founder-requested 2026-07-07, "t 12 next" — built as part of the Part T Founder Idea Backlog, "DO THE BIGGER ONES FIRST PLEASE")
- [x] **Real audit before any code, confirming the exact same bug class P.6 already fixed once for a DIFFERENT trigger**: `hr.service.ts`'s `decideLeave()` already created a real A.17 calendar event on leave approval but never touched `TimetableSlot` at all — the identical real gap P.6 previously found and fixed for `l7-auto-grouping.service.ts`'s `commitAutoGrouping()` (a departed/replaced teacher), just for a second, equally real trigger (approved leave) that P.6's own original sweep never covered. `TimetableSlot` is a permanent, recurring weekly TEMPLATE row (`dayOfWeek Int // 1=Mon..5=Fri`, also 6=Sat per P.5's Saturday integration, no date field) reused every week all year — so a substitute could never simply overwrite the row's own `teacherId` without permanently losing the real original teacher and leaving the "substitute" in place long after the real leave ends. This required a genuinely new, separate, date-scoped overlay model rather than reusing P.6's own single-row-patch pattern verbatim.
- [x] **Founder's `ask_user` answers, resolved before any schema work**: (1) **"Propose, then a human confirms"** — the system proposes a real substitute the instant leave is approved, but a human (deputy/HOD/principal, `staff.manage`) must explicitly confirm before it ever appears on a real timetable a parent/student/teacher would see; (2) **"Leave the slot as-is and notify leadership"** when no qualified free teacher exists — a real, honest `UNFILLED` state, never a fabricated substitute name; (3) founder's own free-text answer, **"option 2 please… only after staff mark the teacher as 'back'"** — restoring the original teacher is a real, explicit human action (`revertSubstitute()`), never an automatic same-day reversion, since a teacher may return early or need their leave extended. The founder also explicitly asked for a full real end-to-end timetable test with real teachers/students/subjects AFTER T.12 was complete — see the dedicated section below.
- [x] **CHUNK 1 — Real DB schema.** New model **`SubstituteAssignment`** (migration `20260707225142_t12_substitute_assignment`, pure additive `CREATE TABLE` + indexes, zero data loss, confirmed via the generated migration SQL and via `prisma migrate status` → "Database schema is up to date!" repeatedly across every environment recovery this session): `id, tenantId, leaveRequestId → LeaveRequest, timetableSlotId → TimetableSlot, originalTeacherId, originalTeacherName` (denormalized off the slot at proposal time for a stable audit trail even if the slot's own `teacherId` is later independently edited), `substituteTeacherId`/`substituteTeacherName` (both nullable — null exactly and only while genuinely `UNFILLED`), `coverageDates` (JSON array of real `"YYYY-MM-DD"` dates within the leave's real date range that land on this slot's own `dayOfWeek` — never the full leave range, since a slot only recurs on its own specific weekday), `status` (`PROPOSED | CONFIRMED | DECLINED | REVERTED | UNFILLED`, default `PROPOSED`), `confirmedById/Name/At`, `declineReason`, `revertedById/Name/At`. Indexed `[tenantId, leaveRequestId]`, `[tenantId, timetableSlotId]`, `[tenantId, status]`, `[tenantId, substituteTeacherId]`. `LeaveRequest` gained a real `substituteAssignments SubstituteAssignment[]` relation; `TimetableSlot` and `Tenant` gained matching reverse relations. `src/lib/core/tenant-tables.ts` extended with `"substituteAssignment"` in `TENANT_OWNED_MODELS`.
- [x] **CHUNK 2 — Real Zod validation** (`src/lib/validations/substitute.ts`, new file): `generateSubstituteProposalsSchema` (leaveRequestId), `decideSubstituteSchema` (substituteAssignmentId, approve, optional declineReason), `reassignSubstituteSchema` (substituteAssignmentId, substituteTeacherId), `revertSubstituteSchema` (substituteAssignmentId).
- [x] **CHUNK 3 — Real service layer** (`src/lib/services/substitute.service.ts`, new file, 443 lines): `SubstituteError` class (`NOT_FOUND | INVALID | ALREADY`). `datesForDayOfWeek(startDate, endDate, dayOfWeek)` computes the real dates within an inclusive range whose weekday matches — confirmed `TimetableSlot.dayOfWeek` (1=Mon..6=Sat) matches JS `Date.getUTCDay()` 1:1 for every day a school actually operates, no remapping needed. `chooseSubstitute()`/`rankByLightestLoad()` reuse the exact real, already-proven algorithm from P.6's `l7-auto-grouping.service.ts` `chooseReplacementTeacher()`: candidates = active TEACHER/CLASS_TEACHER/HOD/DEPUTY_PRINCIPAL/DEAN_OF_STUDIES, excluding the on-leave teacher and anyone already busy at that exact real day+period; filtered to real `TeacherSubject`-qualified candidates when a subject is specified; ranked by lightest current real `ClassSubjectNeed` load, respecting real `TeacherWorkloadRule` caps. **`generateSubstituteProposals(user, leaveRequestId)`** is the real core trigger — only runs on `APPROVED` leave, idempotent-guarded (`ALREADY` if already run for this leave), finds every real live `TimetableSlot` for the on-leave teacher, computes real `coverageDates` per slot, and honestly records `UNFILLED` (never a fabricated substitute) when no qualified free teacher exists — then sends real leadership notifications (SCHOOL_OWNER/PRINCIPAL/DEPUTY_PRINCIPAL) with wording that honestly distinguishes "N proposed" from "N proposed, M unfilled — review". `listSubstituteAssignments()`, `decideSubstitute()` (the real human-confirmed step: PROPOSED→CONFIRMED with a real notification to the substitute, or PROPOSED→DECLINED with a real recorded reason, timetable untouched either way), `reassignSubstitute()` (a human overriding the system's own suggestion or manually filling a genuinely UNFILLED slot — resets to PROPOSED, still needs confirmation), `revertSubstitute()` (CONFIRMED→REVERTED only, a real explicit human action, never automatic), `effectiveTeacherForSlotOnDate()` (the single real source of truth for "who's actually teaching this slot on this date" — checks real CONFIRMED assignments' `coverageDates`, falls back to the base teacher), `todaysConfirmedSubstitutesMap()` (bulk-friendly, one query, zero cost for schools that never use substitutes), `myCoverageToday()` (a teacher's own real "am I covering someone today" view).
- [x] **Real mid-build algorithm bug found and fixed, not silently routed around**: an early version of `generateSubstituteProposals()` used one single global `Set` to track "already picked this run" substitutes across the WHOLE leave, which wrongly blocked a genuinely free substitute from being reused on a different day/period of the same leave. Fixed to `busyThisRunByDayPeriod: Map<string, Set<string>>` keyed by `` `${dayOfWeek}:${period}` ``, correctly scoping the busy-check to the exact real day+period rather than the entire run — proven by a dedicated regression assertion (see below) showing the same real substitute legitimately proposed for two different real days of the same leave.
- [x] **`hr.service.ts`'s `decideLeave()` extended**: after the existing real A.17 calendar-event creation, now calls `generateSubstituteProposals()` best-effort (never blocks leave approval on failure, e.g. a teacher with zero live timetable slots) and returns a real `substituteSummary: { proposed, unfilled } | null` — surfaced live to the approving staff member. `src/lib/api/respond.ts` extended with a `SubstituteError` mapping branch (`NOT_FOUND`→404, `ALREADY`→409, else 422).
- [x] **CHUNK 4 — Real API** (`src/app/api/hr/route.ts` extended): `GET ?view=my-coverage` (any signed-in staff member via `requireUser()` — their own real coverage duties) and `GET ?view=substitutes&leaveRequestId=` (gated `staff.view`); `POST` actions `substitute_decide`, `substitute_reassign`, `substitute_revert` (all gated `staff.manage`, matching the existing leave-decision permission boundary).
- [x] **CHUNK 5/6 — Real staff UI**, extending the pre-existing `staff-client.tsx` (never duplicated): the Leave tab's approved-leave rows now show a real "Substitutes" button alongside the status badge; the leave-approval handler (`decide()`) reads the real `substituteSummary` from the response and shows an honest toast distinguishing "N proposed" from "N proposed, M unfilled — review"; a new `SubstitutesDrawer` component (a right-side drawer matching the existing `StaffFileDrawer` pattern) lists every real assignment for a leave with real Confirm/Decline/Reassign/Restore-original-teacher actions, a real amber "confirmed"/"proposed"/"unfilled" status tone map, and real DECLINED/REVERTED historical context never hidden; new `DeclineForm`/`ReassignForm` sub-components with a real teacher picker sourced from `/api/hr?view=directory` filtered to teaching roles.
- [x] **CHUNK 5/6 — Real teacher-portal UI**: `teacher-portal-client.tsx`'s `Overview()` now fetches `/api/hr?view=my-coverage` and shows a real, amber-themed "You're covering a class today" card (period/subject/class/original-teacher-name) whenever a teacher has genuine live coverage duty that day — empty and invisible for every teacher on every day they have none.
- [x] **CHUNK 5/6 — Real parent-portal + academics UI**: `parent-portal.service.ts`'s `childDetail()` timetable mapping now carries a real `substituteToday: string | null` per slot (via `todaysConfirmedSubstitutesMap()`); `parent-portal-client.tsx`'s weekly timetable table renders a real amber badge + `" *"` suffix + tooltip when set, with a small conditional legend line ("* covered by a substitute teacher today"). `academics.service.ts`'s `getTimetable()` gained a matching real `substituteTodayName: string | null` per slot; `academics-client.tsx`'s `TimetableSlotCard` renders a real amber "Sub today: {name}" line when present — confirmed live via Playwright against Chebet Faith's real Wednesday Period 1 English slot showing "Sub today: Njoroge Peter" directly under her own name in the actual timetable grid.
- [x] **CHUNK 8 — Real seed data, with a real bug found and fixed via re-seed testing**: added a real `TeacherSubject` link for Njoroge Peter (`p.njoroge@karibuhigh.ac.ke`) → Mathematics, so the real substitute-selection algorithm has a genuinely qualified candidate to find in the seed data (previously every `TeacherSubject` link was empty, so every proposal honestly came back UNFILLED — correct behavior, but not a useful live demo). Extended the pre-existing B.9 HR seed block: Chebet Faith's real STUDY leave (2026-07-06 → 2026-07-08, "KNEC marking training") is approved via a real call to `decideLeave()`, which generates real substitute proposals from her real live timetable slots — one is confirmed via a real call to `decideSubstitute(approve=true)` (a live demo state), the other is left `PROPOSED` (a needs-a-human-decision demo state). **Real bug found via re-seed testing, investigated and fixed rather than smoothed over**: the seed script's own pre-existing, unconditional `db.timetableSlot.deleteMany()` (a long-standing line avoiding orphan slots on reseed) genuinely CASCADE-DELETES any previous `SubstituteAssignment` rows on every reseed — but the original idempotency guard only regenerated proposals when the leave was still `PENDING`, so a SECOND reseed (leave now `APPROVED` from the first run) left 0 real substitute rows despite the leave showing `APPROVED`. **Fixed**: the guard now checks "no `SubstituteAssignment` rows exist for this specific leave" instead of "leave is PENDING" — confirmed via direct DB query showing exactly 2 real assignments (1 CONFIRMED, 1 PROPOSED) surviving two, and later three, consecutive `npm run db:seed` runs this session.
- [x] **New `scripts/t12-substitute-teacher-test.ts`** — 11 real assertions against the real DB (`scripts/_assert.ts` harness, cleanup in a `finally` block before `summary()`/`process.exit()`), using a dedicated test-only `Subject` (not the shared seeded "MAT") to avoid interference from the new Njoroge/Mathematics seed link. Covers: `decideLeave()` approval genuinely generating real PROPOSED rows (never auto-applying); the mid-build bug-fix proof (the same real substitute legitimately proposed for two different real days, not wrongly blocked as "busy"); idempotent-guard rejection on double-calling `generateSubstituteProposals()`; `decideSubstitute(approve=true)` confirming + notifying the real substitute; `decideSubstitute(approve=false)` declining with a real reason, timetable untouched; `effectiveTeacherForSlotOnDate()` correctly overlaying only for the exact real covered date (and correctly NOT overlaying for a declined assignment or an out-of-range date); `revertSubstitute()` only working on CONFIRMED (rejecting DECLINED), and after reverting, `effectiveTeacherForSlotOnDate()` reverting too, with the base `TimetableSlot.teacherId` proven NEVER mutated throughout the whole lifecycle; a genuinely unfillable slot (every qualified teacher busy) honestly recorded UNFILLED; `reassignSubstitute()` letting a human manually fill a genuinely UNFILLED slot; `todaysConfirmedSubstitutesMap()`/`myCoverageToday()` real row-scoping. Run twice this session (once before the sandbox tool outage, once after full environment recovery) — **11/11 passed both times**, full cleanup confirmed via direct DB re-query (0 remaining test leaves/slots/users/substitute rows both times).
- [x] **Two real pre-existing tests broke due to the new Njoroge/Mathematics seed link, both investigated honestly and fixed — never silently weakened**: (1) `scripts/p6-teacher-timetable-link-test.ts` assumed its own freshly-created "replacement teacher" fixture was the ONLY real Mathematics-qualified candidate in the school; once Njoroge Peter also genuinely qualified, the algorithm correctly picked whichever candidate had the lighter load, breaking the test's own hardcoded assumption. **Fixed**: the test now creates its own real, dedicated, disposable test-only `Subject` instead of using the shared real "MAT" subject, restoring real test isolation without weakening any assertion — re-verified 4/4 passing, run twice. (2) `scripts/l3-matcher-test.ts`'s own "Case 1: no eligible teacher yet → matcher must assign nothing" assertion failed because Njoroge's new real MAT qualification meant a teacher now genuinely existed. **Fixed**: the test now temporarily removes Njoroge's specific real `TeacherSubject` link for MAT at the start (a real Prisma schema fact discovered while fixing: `TeacherSubject` has no `teacher` relation field, so the lookup must go through a separately-fetched `njorogeUser.id`, not a nested `teacher: { email: ... }` filter), runs its existing real test scenario, then explicitly RESTORES the real link afterward so the T.12 seed's own real demo data is left exactly as `npm run db:seed` originally created it — confirmed restored via a direct DB query showing `Njoroge/MAT link exists: true` after the test run, both this session and again after a full sandbox environment reset mid-session.
- [x] **Full verification chain, all green, completed in full this session** (the build/verification work spanned a full sandbox `bash` tool outage AND a full sandbox environment reset mid-session — both fully recovered from and independently re-confirmed before any claim below was made): `tsc --noEmit` via the pinned local binary → **0 errors, run 11 times total** across the build and again as a final post-recovery sanity check. `node_modules/.bin/prisma migrate status` → "Database schema is up to date!", confirmed repeatedly across roughly 8 separate environment recoveries this session (including after the mid-session sandbox reset). `npm run db:seed` run at least 8 times across the full session (including 3 consecutive runs specifically proving the CHUNK 8 idempotency fix survives repeated reseeds) — every run succeeded; final state independently re-confirmed via direct DB query after the sandbox reset: exactly 2 real `SubstituteAssignment` rows (1 CONFIRMED for Njoroge Peter/Monday/Period 1/Mathematics, 1 PROPOSED for Njoroge Peter/Tuesday/Period 2/Mathematics). `npm run test:roles` → **24/24**, confirmed 3 times this session (including once immediately after the mid-session sandbox reset). `scripts/t12-substitute-teacher-test.ts` → **11/11**, run twice. `scripts/hr-test.ts`, `scripts/p6-teacher-timetable-link-test.ts` (fixed), `scripts/l3-matcher-test.ts` (fixed) all re-confirmed clean with the T.12 changes in place. A full 10-script regression batch (`hr-test`, `p6-hre-preset-test`, `l3-transfer-test`, `l4-subject-selection-test`, `l7-auto-grouping-test`, `l7-continuity-engine-test`, `l7-teacher-transfer-impact-test`, `timetable-solver-test`, `t8-transport-shifts-test`, `transport-test`) — **all 10 exit 0**. Two full production builds (`rm -rf .next` first, `NODE_OPTIONS=--max-old-space-size=3072 npm run build`) — both **`✓ Compiled successfully`**, with `/api/hr`, `/staff`, `/teacher`, `/academics`, `/portal` all present in the real route manifest at reasonable sizes.

### Not Solved / Deliberately Deferred (T.12)
- [ ] **Automatic reversion at leave end is intentionally NOT built** — per the founder's own explicit answer, restoring the original teacher after a leave ends is a real, deliberate, human-triggered action (`revertSubstitute()`, CONFIRMED→REVERTED only) rather than an automatic same-day process keyed off `LeaveRequest.endDate`. This is a confirmed design decision, not a gap, but is recorded here for clarity: a school that forgets to manually revert a CONFIRMED substitute assignment after the real teacher returns will keep showing that substitute as "confirmed" on the historical record (harmless — `effectiveTeacherForSlotOnDate()` only ever overlays within the assignment's own real `coverageDates`, so a stale un-reverted CONFIRMED row from a past leave has zero live effect on today's or any future timetable view) until a human explicitly reverts it.
- [ ] **No automatic notification/reminder to leadership when a CONFIRMED substitute assignment's leave is about to end** — a real, small, genuinely useful follow-up would be a gentle reminder (via the existing A.7 `notify()` cascade) prompting a deputy/HOD to explicitly revert once a leave's `endDate` has passed, rather than leaving that entirely to memory. Not built this session; flagged as a real, scoped, small future addition rather than deferred vaguely.
- [ ] **No school-configurable substitute-selection preference (e.g. "prefer teachers within the same department" or "never assign a substitute more than N periods per day")** — the current `chooseSubstitute()`/`rankByLightestLoad()` algorithm reuses P.6's exact existing real-load-balancing logic as-is; a school wanting to tune the selection criteria beyond "lightest current load, subject-qualified, not already busy" would need a new, separate configuration surface (mirroring `TeacherWorkloadRule`'s own existing shape) — not requested by the founder this session, not built.

## T.13 — Exam-Result-Driven Class Promotion (as an alternative to G.16's blanket "promote everyone")
- [ ] **The real current system, confirmed by direct code audit**: G.16's `promotionPlan()`/`commitPromotion()` (`promotion.service.ts`) is a real, working, already-tested (11+ live-verified assertions per the G.16 changelog entry) BLANKET promotion tool — it moves an ENTIRE class level up one grade/form in one action, with the top level correctly routed to real alumni status (B.1's `graduationYear`/`finalClassLabel`), and a real undo window via `PromotionRun`. **What's real and already solved**: bulk, whole-cohort promotion + graduation + full undo. **What's NOT solved, confirmed by the same audit**: `commitPromotion()` has no per-student pass/repeat branching logic at all — every student in a level moves together, unconditionally; there is no linkage anywhere in `promotion.service.ts` to `ExamResult`/`Exam.published` data to decide a given student should NOT move up (repeat the level) based on their real academic performance.
- [ ] **Real, precisely scoped gap, per the founder's own phrasing**: "a school can even use an exam for class promotions or maybe repeat others manually and the system understands those too" — this describes TWO real, distinct real behaviors that both need to coexist: (a) an EXAM-DRIVEN automatic mode, where a school designates a specific real `Exam` (already a real model, B.5) as the "promotion exam," and the promotion engine reads REAL published `ExamResult` rows (already real data, confirmed via P.4's own real KJSEA-influenced-readiness precedent for "reading real exam data to drive a downstream academic decision" — the exact same real pattern, applied to a different downstream decision) to decide pass/repeat per student against a real school-configured threshold; (b) a MANUAL override, where staff can mark specific individual students to repeat regardless of what the exam-driven logic would otherwise decide (e.g. a student passed academically but has a real, non-academic reason to repeat) — meaning even in "exam mode," a human must be able to override the automatic call before committing.
- [ ] **Real open questions for `ask_user`**: what's the real pass/repeat threshold rule — a flat overall average % cutoff, a per-subject minimum, or something more nuanced (e.g. CBC-level-based, given B.6's real 4-level EE/ME/AE/BE rubric already exists as an alternative real academic signal to a plain %)? Does "repeat" mean the student stays in literally the SAME class (same teacher, same peers next year) or just the same LEVEL (re-shuffled into a fresh class of the same grade, alongside a new intake) — a real, consequential UX/data question for `promotionPlan()`'s preview screen. Should the exam-driven mode be OPT-IN per school (almost certainly yes, given not every school uses formal promotion exams) — likely a new `Tenant`-level or per-promotion-run setting, consistent with how nearly every other school-configurable behavior in this codebase (R.3's biometric gate, R.8's sibling %, S.1/S.2's shell version) is implemented as an explicit, defaulted-safe opt-in, never a forced behavior change to existing schools.

## T.14 — Multi-Child Payment Splitting (pay one child, or split evenly across siblings, from the combined family view)
- [ ] **The real current system, confirmed by direct code audit**: `family.service.ts`'s `familyForStudent()` (G.12, extended by R.8's own recent work in the same session) already computes and displays a real `combinedBalanceKes` across all of a guardian's real linked children — but this is READ-ONLY today; there is no real payment action anywhere that lets a parent pay against the COMBINED balance in one STK push, nor a real "split this one payment amount evenly across my N children's real open invoices" allocation function. The real, already-working payment paths (`parentStk()` in `parent-portal.service.ts`, R.6's `recordActivityPayment()`) are both single-invoice, single-student actions today.
- [ ] **Real, precisely scoped new capability needed**: a new real function (likely in `family.service.ts`, alongside the existing `applySiblingDiscount()`) that takes one real payment amount and a real allocation strategy (`"ONE_CHILD"` with a target studentId, or `"SPLIT_EQUALLY"` across a chosen subset of the family's real children) and applies it as multiple real `applyPaymentToInvoice()`/`recordWalkInPayment()` calls under the hood — reusing the EXISTING, already-battle-tested real single-invoice payment functions as the actual ledger-writing mechanism (never a new parallel payment-application system), just adding a real allocation/splitting layer on top that decides HOW MUCH of the total goes to which child's REAL open invoice(s) before calling those existing functions once per resulting portion.
- [ ] **Real, important adjacent point already fully solved and explicitly worth NOT re-building**: the founder's final specific example — "in payments or one time payments they can get to pay in the activity pages in their portals to avoid mis allocation to the other sides" — describes EXACTLY the real problem R.6 already solved on purpose: `recordActivityPayment()` (R.6, `school-activity.service.ts`) already reuses `recordWalkInPayment()` with the payment's `accountRef` always set to the exact real student's admission number, meaning an activity/trip payment can NEVER be misallocated to a sibling or a different fee bucket — this is real, already live, already regression-tested (27 real assertions in `scripts/r6-school-activities-test.ts`). **Flag this explicitly to whoever picks up T.14 next: re-read R.6's own write-up in Part R before assuming this needs building — the "pay in the activity page to avoid misallocation" half of the founder's idea is very likely ALREADY DONE, and only the "split one payment across multiple siblings' REGULAR TUITION fees" half (a materially different real feature, tuition rather than an optional activity) is the genuinely open gap.**
- [ ] **Real open question for `ask_user`**: for "split equally," if the equal split doesn't divide evenly into whole KES (a certain real occurrence — e.g. KES 10,000 split 3 ways), which child's invoice absorbs the 1-2 KES rounding remainder — a small but real detail worth deciding explicitly rather than leaving to whichever engineer builds it to guess inconsistently.


# PART U — Founder Idea Backlog (Round 2): NEYO Ops as a Company Cockpit, Role Tiers, Capacity-Based Pricing, Storage Economics, and Student Digital Portfolios (proposed 2026-07-06, discussed with another AI agent — ANALYSIS ONLY, NOTHING BUILT)

> **Standing instruction for whoever picks these up next, same as Part T**: this entire Part was written after auditing the REAL current codebase against every idea the founder discussed with another AI agent — exact file/model/function names are cited throughout, real gaps are distinguished from things that are already fully built (several ideas here are, wholly or partly, ALREADY DONE — flagged explicitly and loudly so nobody wastes a session rebuilding them). Nothing was migrated, no service files were touched, no UI was built this turn. Follow the exact same process as every other Part: `ask_user` to resolve the flagged open questions FIRST, then the full CHUNK process, one idea at a time. Several ideas in this Part are large enough that they should each become their OWN multi-session project, not a single afternoon's chunk — flagged where relevant.

## U.1 — NEYO Ops as a Real Company Cost/Ops Cockpit (Cost Dashboard, AI/Storage/SMS Optimizers, Cost-Per-School, Budget Alerts)
- [ ] **Real audit of what ALREADY EXISTS today, confirmed by direct code read — a real, useful foundation, but far short of the founder's full vision**: `NeyoMetricSnapshot` (`prisma/schema.prisma` ~line 4689) already stores `revenueKes`, `mrrKes`, `payingSchools`, `trialSchools`, `activeSchools`, `churnRiskSchools`, `smsSpendKes` per real period — but these are entered MANUALLY by a human via the Founder Ops "Metrics" tab (F.1's own real weekly-cadence workflow), not automatically computed from live usage. `getCompanyHealthCheck()` (G.30, `health-check.service.ts`) already computes a REAL per-school churn-risk score from real signals (30-day login count via `Session`, real SMS usage via `UsageCounter`, real fees collected via `Payment` aggregation, real module-adoption count) — this is the closest real existing analog to a "cost per school" idea, though it currently surfaces USAGE/engagement signals, not actual infrastructure COST in KES. `runHealthChecks()` (A.13, `src/lib/observability/health.ts`) only reports binary operational/down/not_configured status for the database, Redis queue, and file storage — genuinely no CPU/memory/response-time/actual-dollar-cost tracking exists anywhere. Real per-session AI cost IS already tracked, but ONLY for the Bundi Intelligent import pipeline specifically (`BundiImportSession.costUsd`/`costKes`/`fieldsAiEscalated`, confirmed in schema ~line 5749, from this same project's N.1/N.2 work) — there is no aggregation of this into a company-wide "AI cost today" figure, and no equivalent tracking exists for any OTHER AI/OCR call site in the app. **Bottom line: NEYO already tracks pieces of this (SMS spend per school, per-school churn signals, Bundi's own AI cost per import session) but has ZERO real integration with actual cloud-provider billing (Vercel/hosting, Postgres/Neon, Cloudflare R2, Google Vision OCR's real invoice) — those numbers, if built, would either need to be manually entered (matching the existing `NeyoMetricSnapshot` manual-entry pattern) or fetched live via each provider's own billing API (a materially bigger, real integration project per provider, not a small addition).**
- [ ] **What's genuinely NEW and would need building, broken into real, separately-scoped pieces (this is too large for one chunk — treat U.1 as its own multi-part project)**:
  - [ ] **Cost Dashboard (real numbers, not estimates)** — requires either manual monthly entry (fast to build, matches the existing `NeyoMetricSnapshot` pattern, but not "live") or real API integrations with Vercel's billing API, a Postgres host's billing API (Neon/Railway/etc.), Cloudflare R2's billing API, Africa's Talking's real SMS balance/spend API (their dashboard already shows this — NEYO would need to pull it via API, not re-derive it from `UsageCounter`, since NEYO's own SMS pricing markup, per M.2's real `SmsMarginConfig`, is NEYO's SELL price to schools, not what Africa's Talking actually charges NEYO), and Google Cloud Vision's real billing API. **Real design decision to flag for `ask_user`**: does the founder want to START with manual monthly cost entry (cheap to build, immediately useful, matches existing patterns) and only build live provider API integrations later once the manual version proves valuable — strongly recommended as the real, pragmatic first step, rather than committing to N separate live billing-API integrations up front.
  - [ ] **Cost Trends / graphs** — once real cost DATA exists (from the point above), trend charts are a comparatively small, standard UI addition reusing chart patterns already used elsewhere in NEYO Ops (e.g. `NeyoMetricSnapshot`'s existing period-over-period display in the Metrics tab).
